## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by time t and current population size P, matching classical continuous-time population dynamics (ODE) models with density dependence and time-varying forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (secular change in per-capita growth over time)
- Power-law (allometric) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear scaling of growth with population size)
- Linear density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; quadratic self-limitation)
- Logistic differential equation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity-limited growth in ODE form)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density dependence strength/shape)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with logarithmic density regulation)
- Allee effect (strong/weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low density plus carrying capacity)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-limited growth with constant per-capita removal)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (density-limited growth with fixed removal)
- Seasonally forced per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting growth)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (density dependence plus seasonal forcing)
- Immigration/emigration forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (external influx/efflux changing over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth diagnostics: if dP_dt / P is ~constant, expect dP_dt ∝ P; if it decreases with P, include negative P**2 or logistic-type factors
- Carrying capacity signature: zeros at P=0 and at a positive P imply multiplicative structure P*(1 - c*P) or P*(1 - (c*P)**theta)
- Crowding vs. depensation: negative curvature at high P suggests self-limitation (−P**2); a sign change from negative to positive at low P suggests an Allee factor (c*P − 1)
- Gompertz vs logistic separation: if per-capita growth declines roughly linearly with log(P), prefer P*log(K/P) over P*(1 - c*P)
- Seasonality: oscillations in dP_dt at similar P values across time suggest adding sin(c*t + phase) to the per-capita rate
- Harvesting/removal: persistent negative shift in dP_dt across P suggests subtracting a constant term; removal proportional to population suggests subtracting c*P
- Non-integer density effects: if growth suppression strengthens abruptly with P, use theta-logistic (1 - (c*P)**theta) rather than simple (1 - c*P)
- Regime change in time: systematic drift in growth rate over t indicates r(t) forms like c0 + c1*t or exp(c*t) multiplying P

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG16)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6 + c7*P
Candidate formulas: 59

Let  
\[
\text{GT}(P)=0.8677806610632854\cdot(-1+P/6.0579356272)\cdot(1-P/14.1850527796)\cdot P\;+\;0.8677806610632854\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.8677806610632854\,P.
\]
GT depends **only on \(P\)** (no \(t\)). Expand the cubic part:
\[
(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P = \big(-1 + P/a + P/b - P^2/(ab)\big)P
= -P + (1/a+1/b)P^2 - (1/(ab))P^3.
\]
Multiplying by \(k=0.8677806610632854\) and adding \(kP\) cancels the \(-kP\) term exactly, so GT simplifies to
\[
\text{GT}(P)= k\,P^{1/3} \;+\; k(1/a+1/b)P^2 \;-\; k(1/(ab))P^3,
\]
with **no constant term and no linear \(P\) term**.

Compute the needed coefficients:

```python
k=0.8677806610632854
a=6.057935627201261
b=14.185052779605893
coef2=k*(1/a+1/b)
coef3=-k*(1/(a*b))
coef2,coef3
```

```python
0.2054543892945209 -0.010103253835591625
```

So
\[
\text{GT}(P)=0.8677806610632854\,P^{1/3} + 0.2054543892945209\,P^2 - 0.010103253835591625\,P^3.
\]

A candidate can match GT iff it can be parameter-set to exactly this combination (only \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\) terms; no \(t\)-dependence; no other powers; no constant; no linear term).

### Candidate-by-candidate

1. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P\cdot c3(Pc4)^{c5} + P c6\sin(\cdots)\)  
   Has a sine-in-\(t\) term unless \(c6=0\). Then remaining terms are \(P^3\), \(P^2\), and \(P^{1+c5}\). No way to produce \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

2. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + c3 + c4\sin(\cdots)\)  
   Set \(c4=0\) to remove \(t\). But there is an unavoidable constant \(c3\) unless set \(c3=0\) (ok). Then we have exactly \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). Choose
   - \(c0 = 0.8677806610632854\)
   - \(c2 = 0.2054543892945209\)
   - \(c1 = -0.010103253835591625\)
   - \(c3=0\), \(c4=0\)  
   This equals GT. **Match**.

3. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3 + P^{c4}c5 + c6 t + c7 + c8 e^{c9 t}\)  
   To remove \(t\): need \(c6=0\) and \(c8=0\) (or \(c9=0\) still leaves \(e^0=1\) constant). Still has linear \(Pc1\) unless \(c1=0\), and has constant \(c7\) unless \(c7=0\). Could set exponents \(c2=1/3\), \(c4=3\) to get needed powers, but then you’d have \(P^2\) plus two extra power terms—actually that could work if you use \(P^2c0\) for the \(P^2\) coefficient and use \(P^{c2}c3\) and \(P^{c4}c5\) for \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^3\). Yes, but there is no obstruction after setting \(c1=c6=c7=c8=0\). Then set:
   - \(c0=0.2054543892945209\)
   - \(c2=1/3,\; c3=0.8677806610632854\)
   - \(c4=3,\; c5=-0.010103253835591625\)  
   This matches GT. **Match**.

4. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + c3 + c4\log(c5 e^{P^{c6}c7 + c8 t}+1)\)  
   The log term depends on \(P\) and/or \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Then it reduces to candidate 14 form with extra constant \(c3\) removable by \(c3=0\). Then it can match like candidate 2. **Match** (set \(c4=0,c3=0\) and pick \(c0,c1,c2\) as above).

5. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + c3 + c4 e^{c5 t}\)  
   Remove \(t\) by \(c4=0\). Then constant \(c3\) must be 0. Remaining \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\) can match. **Match**.

6. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P c3(Pc4)^{c5} + P^{c6}c7\log(Pc8+1)\)  
   Log term cannot become a pure power for all \(P\) unless coefficient \(c7=0\). Then no \(P^{1/3}\) term. **No match**.

7. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P c3(Pc4)^{c5} + c6 e^{c7 t}\)

9. exp(t)*log(P…) term must be killed with \(c6=0\); then no \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

10. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t} + c6\)

11. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3\)  
    Combine \(P^2\) coefficients: \(c2+c3\). Choose \(c0,k\) and \(c1\) and \(c2+c3\) to match. **Match**.

12. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2(c2+c3+c4) + c5\)

13. Has \(P^3(c1+c2)\) and \(P^2(c3+c4+c5)\) plus \(P^{1/3}c0\) and constant \(c6\). Set \(c6=0\). Then match. **Match**.

15. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2(c2+c3) + c4\)

16. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + P c4(Pc5)^{c6}\)

Can’t create \(P^{1/3}\) (would require \(1+c6=1/3\Rightarrow c6=-2/3\), giving \(P^{1/3}\) yes, but then it is multiplied by \(c4 c5^{c6}\) and still we’d be missing the explicit \(P^{1/3}\) term? Actually that would *be* a \(P^{1/3}\) term. However then we still have only \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) and \(P^{1/3}\): that seems promising. But note the \(P^3c0\) term exists, good; \(P^2\) exists, good; and \(P^{1/3}\) can be produced by setting \(c6=-2/3\). Yes, so it can match by:

    **Match**.

25. Contains \(P^2\), \(P\), \(P^{c2}\), plus a rational term \(P^{c4}c5/(P^{c4}+c6)\) and \(t\)-exp term. Kill \(t\) by \(c8=0\). Kill rational by \(c5=0\). Kill linear and constant by \(c1=0,c7=0\). Then left with \(P^2c0 + P^{c2}c3\): cannot produce both \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^3\). **No match**.

26. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P c3(Pc4)^{c5} + P c6\)

28. Has \(P^3\), \(P^2\), \(P c6\) and \(P c7(Pc8)^{c9}\). Need no linear term: set \(c6=0\). Use last term with \(c9=-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Then match. **Match**.

29. Like 26 but with extra \(P c7\). Set \(c6=0,c7=0\), set \(c5=-2/3\). **Match**.

30. Has extra \(P c7/(P+c8)\) which is not a polynomial/power term unless killed: set \(c7=0\). Also has linear terms \(P c6\) and \(P c9\): set \(c6=0,c9=0\). Then reduce to 18 and match with \(c5=-2/3\). **Match**.

36. Contains rational terms \(P c4/(P+c5)\) and \(P^{c6}c7/(P^{c6}+c8)\); must set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\) to remove them, and constant \(c9=0\). Then left with \(P^3,P^2,P\) only—no \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

37. Has \(P c3\) plus two power terms \(P^{1+c6}\) and \(P^{1+c9}\). You can set \(c3=0\), set one exponent to \(-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\), but then you still need a \(P^2\) term: none unless you set the other exponent to 1 (giving \(P^2\)), yes. Then you still need \(P^3\) and it exists. So set \(c6=-2/3\) (for \(P^{1/3}\)) and \(c9=1\) (for \(P^2\)). Works. **Match**.

    Remove \(t\) by \(c5=0\). Remove linear and constant by \(c1=0,c7=0\). Left with \(P^2\) and one power \(P^{c2}\): cannot also produce \(P^3\). **No match**.
